text:
I don't know what the others were talking about.  This was a great recipe.  I used honey mustard instead of dijon and honey teriyaki barbecue sauce instead of plain teriyaki sauce.  But I also used only 4 oz of mustard on 6 whole chicken breasts and I think that helped the mustard not overpower.  The chicken came out so juicy.  I lightly greased the bottom of the pan and my "sauce" didn't burn at all.  And I used real bacon crumbled up to lessen the salt content.  This was perfect with pesto rice. This was an overall great dish!

text:
I am a man who rarely cooks - yet I was able to make this dish with ease and it turned out great.  My wife and I love it and have it once a week.

We've even made it for casual dinner parties with great results.

I follow the recipe to the letter, except I substitute "Dijonaise" (dijon mustard with mayo) for the mustard.  After trying it both ways, I find that the Dijonaise creates jucier results.

As to the bacon, I start with fresh bacon and microwave it crispy and then crumble/chop to make the bits.

Thanks for this wonderful recipe!

text:
Really delicious!  I didn't know if the dijon/teriyaki pairing would work; but it really did.  It might have helped that I didn't use processed bacon bits but instead fried up three strips of bacon for the three chicken breasts I was using, and chopped it up in the magic bullet.  The processed bits are way more expensive and don't taste nearly as good as fresh bacon.  This recipe is great because you don't need to measure, just slop it all on and it will taste great.

I added about 3 oz of dijon mustard and 1 oz of honey mustard, mixed up well and then added 1/2 cup of Teriyaki sauce to the mustard mix.  Once all mixed well, I poured it on 6 chicken breast halves.  Then I put some grated parm cheese on it and 1/4 cup bacon bits and about 1/3 cup reduced fat mozzarella cheese.  I baked it for 30 minutes exactly at 400.  IT WAS PERFECT!!!

text:
So I used this recipe as a base for my own creation...
instead of dijon, I used honey mustard
instead of teriyaki sauce, I used BBQ sauce
instead of parmesan cheese, I used cheddar cheese
instead of the bacon bits, I used the Hidden Valley Ranch dressing with bacon and onion flavor (delish! but high in cals/ fat, so I didn't use too much)

So easy though, just put the chicken in the baking dish, cover each piece with honey mustard and spread over the chicken with spoon or brush. Then zig-zag drizzle each of the BBQ sauce and Ranch over the pieces of chicken, then sprinkle cheddar cheese on top. Cook at 400 degrees for about 30-50 min depending on the size and type of chicken breasts (we prefer on the bone/ with ribs because it keeps the meat juicy, about 45 min to cook) Made with rice and veggies and our family LOVED it! SOO YUMMY!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
We've been making this for a while now and really enjoy it.  As is, it's a little heavy on the mustard.  I've found that 1 TBS of Dijon per breast is the perfect amount.  I use a thick honey/teriyaki 30-minute marinade in place of regular teriyaki sauce.  You can find it in the BBQ sauce section at the store.  I add a little more teriyaki sauce to the dish as a personal preference.  I combine the cheese and bacon before sprinkling on.  Bake at 375, 45 mins.  To keep the cheese from burning and the chicken moist, I cover the dish with foil and remove about halfway through.  Then I use the juices to baste over the top a couple times before it's done.  Comes out perfect.

I did not follow the recipe amounts, instead I measured per piece of chicken (to be able to figure the points easier). I was skeptical, but my family raved over this tonight!  I did make a few alterations because of what I had on hand...i used 1/2 the mustard called for, then added the same amount in mayo.  Added about 1 tbs brown sugar and a dash of honey...all to cut the strong mustard taste and salt. Shredded mozzarella and broiled to brown.  They loved it over rice and by itself.

text:
WOW!!!  So easy and so tasty!  I was a little skeptical, I even panicked since I made it for 4 lbs. of chicken...  Then I thought I put way too much parmesan cheese.  But it was perfect!  I used about 1/2 Dijon mustard and 1/2 Dijonnaise.  After I washed the chicken, I put it in a bowl with the dijon mixture to coat.  Then I put in a pan and topped with the Teriyaki sauce, and crumbled 6 strips of bacon over it, then COVERED with Parmesan cheese (NOT sprinkled, covered!)  I cooked it at 400 for 45 mins.  Served with stuffing.  I had no idea how much gravy/liquid it would produce (it was alot!)... so that went over the stuffing.  YUMMY!  We will definitely have it again and again; next time I will probably combine the Dijon and Teriyaki and have the chicken marinate a bit.  Thanks, Aimee!!

WOW! What a nice change from blah chicken.After reading the reviews, I mixed the teriyaki and mustard together rather than adding them separately. I was also nervous about the mustard being overpowering, so I used 4oz of dijion mustard for 6 chicken breasts, and probably close to 1/2 cup of reduced sodium teriyaki sauce.I would not recomend a normal sodium content teriyaki- the dish was a bit salty (but not too bad) with the reduced sodium teriyaki. I used fresh parmesan and real bacon. The chicken was super moist and delicious- the flavors blended perfectly. My husband and 7 year old all but licked their plates clean!

text:
I used skin-on, bone-in chicken thighs with this. I thought it was delicious. The mix of flavors was great and the chicken was incredibly moist. I think the chicken skin may temper the saltiness a bit. I think using high quality parmesan cheese is also important for cutting salt. I used 1/4 4c real grated parmesan and 1/4c Kraft. I also used Trader Joe's Soyaki, Hormel Real Bacon. I sprinkled the cheese over the chicken first which I also think it helped keep the saltiness of bacon from overpowering the dish. The bacon bits just added a nice crunch on top. I didn't measure the mustard so but I think I used more like 2 ounces than 4. Fantastic.

Sometimes, time permitting, I marinate the breasts overnight in teriyaki mixed with brown sugar, then coat with the mustard, top with mozzarella and bacon bits and bake. I salt and peppered the chicken, then rubbed a dollop of Dijon mustard on each breast. I don't know that there is an easier dish to make. I have recently become a stay at home mom of 2 & have been trying SEVERAL new recipes & this is the first recipe that said it would take 5 minutes & it really did. I poured 1/2 cup of Dijon Mustard & 1/2 cup of Mayo in a glass measuring cup, stirred together then poured that over my chicken.  I also pierced my chicken with a sharp knife to allow the sauce to seep. I didn't measure my teriyaki sauce, I just drizzled it over the top of the chicken so it was not too salty. Between the taste & simplicity this will definately be made in our house again. Thanks a million, Aimee!

Excellent!!!  I made this for my husband and one of his friends and they both were praising me.  I used half mustard and half Miracle Whip at others suggestion and thought it was perfect.  It was not salty in the slightest.  I used Lawry's Teriyaki sauce, Miracle Whip, Grey Pupon, Hormel Bacon bits (the real kind), and freshly grated Kraft Parm cheese (added 10 minutes before it was done baking). text:
I made this tonight for my family, as well. I took everyone's advice and used a low sodium marinade. I only had 3 chicken breast so I mixed 1/2 cup of marinade with 1/4 cup dijon throughly then coated the chicken. I also used crisp fresh bacon instead of bacon bits and freshly grated parmasan. I layered the chicken as directed, but wrapped each individual breast in its own piece of foil to keep the parmasan from overcooking. Combined with some buttered rice and steamed veggies - it made a wonderful (out of the oridinary) supper. Thanks for the recipe Aimee.

text:
I used Teriyaki sauce/marinade (thicker) and Grey Poupon Country Style Dijon mustard.  I agree with others, it is a bit salty.  Tip: to keep fresh parmasean.  I have a parmasean cheese grater that I place a chunk of cheese into the "wheel" to grate the cheese right on top of the dish.  In order to save from having to clean it every time, I store the whole thing in a plastic bag in the refrigerator.  That way, all I have to do is pull out the plastic bag, grater and cheese, and use on my dish, return to bag and refrigerator.  When the chunk stored in the grater runs out, usually by the 10th meal, I then wash it out and return to refrigerator with a new chunk of high quality parmesean.  Saves alot of clean up time and prep time.

text:
After reading many reviews about the saltiness of the dish, I decided to change things around a bit.  First, I seared the chicken in 2 tbs olive oil for 1 min per side.  I made a mustard mixture consisting of 2 tbs mayo and 2 tbs dijon mustard, which I spread over the chicken after placing them in a baking dish.  I then sprinkled the bacon bits and parm cheese over it and baked as per the original recipie.  I think this will cut down on the saltiness quite a bit, my family did not find it too salty at all.  A good idea for a recipie, but with the bacon bits, parm cheese AND teriaki sauce, it's just way too many salty foods combined.

text:
This is a great, easy recipe. I love the cheese/bacon/mustard combo! My two boys, ages 6 and 10, who can be very picky ate it up too! I marinated my chicken first, with lime, garlic, vinegar/oil overnight. I find if I don't marinate, the chicken is never as good. I also used partially cooked bacon strips, vs the bacon bits. I broiled on low for a few minutes before serving so the bacon was crispy, along with the cheese, and it was yummy! It can be very salty, so choose your teriyaki sauce wisely!

After reading many of the reviews, I decided I would not use as much mustard or teriyaki sauce, but next time, I will use a bit more. I agree w/another review that it's an individual taste thing-I love dijon mustard & the taste is superb! I also bought fresh bacon bits from Hormel...this might make a difference in the taste (or saltiness) of all the ingredients. I am also going to try using grated parmesan with asiago & rosatto to help add some flavor.  Otherwise - what a great, fast dish! My boyfriend loved it & he doesn't like Dijon mustard! Thanks Aimee!
